In 1864 the\u00a0fossil's description was first published in a scientific magazine and official named.<br \/><br \/>However, the find was not the firstNeanderthal\u00a0fossil discovery, rather, the true nature and significance had not been recognized on any of the earlier fossils and therefore no separate species' name was assigned.<br \/><br \/>The discovery was made by\u00a0limestonequarry\u00a0miners. The first description of the remains was made by\u00a0anatomistHermann Schaaffhausen\u00a0and the find was announced jointly in 1857.<br \/><br \/>In 1997, the specimen was the first to yield Neanderthal\u00a0mitochondrial DNAfragments.<br \/><br \/>In 1999, scientists announced that recent excavations had led them to some of the sediments of the now-destroyed cave which contained fragments of Neanderthal bones including one that fit exactly to the original femur.<br \/><br \/>In 2000, the fossil of a second individual from the locality, named\u00a0Neanderthal 2, was identified as a\u00a0Homo neanderthalensis.<br \/><br \/>The Neanderthal 1 publication represents the beginning ofpaleoanthropology\u00a0as a scientific discipline.
